  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4cee7a30-1b6c-456f-ab1d-366895f61026'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer6351256521973100613">Je suis né dans la ville d'Aubagne, sous le Garlaban couronné de chèvres, au temps des derniers chevriers." Ainsi commence l'autobiographie de Marcel Pagnol, immortel auteur de La Trilogie marseillaise, La Femme du boulanger, entre autres savoureuses histoires à l'accent chantant. On découvre ici l'enfance du jeune Marcel et sa découverte des collines enchantées des enviro</span>
  <span id="freeText6351256521973100613" style="display:none">Je suis né dans la ville d'Aubagne, sous le Garlaban couronné de chèvres, au temps des derniers chevriers." Ainsi commence l'autobiographie de Marcel Pagnol, immortel auteur de La Trilogie marseillaise, La Femme du boulanger, entre autres savoureuses histoires à l'accent chantant. On découvre ici l'enfance du jeune Marcel et sa découverte des collines enchantées des environs de Marseille. La famille Pagnol loue pour les vacances une bastide près d'un petit village. Le père de Marcel s'initie à la chasse et sera l'auteur d'un coup de fusil magistral qui lui vaudra l'admiration de tous, à commencer par celle de son fils, et qui donne son titre au livre. Ce premier tome est suivi de deux autres, Le Château de ma mère et Le Temps des secrets. L'incroyable mémoire et le talent de conteur de l'auteur restituent merveilleusement les joies simples, les chagrins énormes, la délicieuse naïveté de l'enfance, sans omettre les tours pendables et bêtises en tous genres qui la ponctuent nécessairement. Une histoire vraie belle comme un roman, bourrée de tendresse et d'émotion, pleine de drôlerie aussi. On lit, on relit, on s'y reconnaît. À travers la sienne, Marcel Pagnol raconte toutes les enfances... du moins telles qu'elles devraient être. --Pascale Wester --Ce texte fait référence à une édition épuisée ou non disponible de ce titre.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6351256521973100613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1503626529?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kalliope" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kalliope" href="/user/show/3593962-kalliope">Kalliope</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3593962-kalliope?shelf=rereads">rereads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3593962-kalliope?shelf=france">france</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3593962-kalliope?shelf=2016">2016</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3593962-kalliope?shelf=travel">travel</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1503626529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1820641288687208874"><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467475002i/19597419._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Recently I discovered what one can do with Google Maps. I used to use it just for looking up places and find my whereabouts. The satellite mode and the homunculus are also fun. But what I love doing now is customise <b>My Maps</b> and keep track of places I have been or want to go. For each recent trip I am now keeping track of the restaurants or shops or less well known places that I visited. I know that no matter how vivid my experience was, with time I will forget the names of the bars, the hotels, </span>
  <span id="freeText1820641288687208874" style="display:none"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467475002i/19597419._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Recently I discovered what one can do with Google Maps. I used to use it just for looking up places and find my whereabouts. The satellite mode and the homunculus are also fun. But what I love doing now is customise <b>My Maps</b> and keep track of places I have been or want to go. For each recent trip I am now keeping track of the restaurants or shops or less well known places that I visited. I know that no matter how vivid my experience was, with time I will forget the names of the bars, the hotels, the monuments.... <br><br>Even for the town I live in now, I am keeping <b>My Tapas &amp; Restaurants Google Map</b>, flagging those that have been recommended to me by various people or magazines, so that in improvised outings or in the evenings after the theatre, I can pull out My Map and try out one of those suggested restaurants.<br><br>For my recent journey to Provence, we were going to visit so many places, small and bigger towns, museums, Roman ruins, restaurants, that to keep track of the busy agenda, and what were we doing each day, I created <b>My Provence Map</b>. So, there I marked Van Gogh’s hospital and yellow café, or Picasso’s mural of Peace, or Cézanne’s studio, or the prehistoric caves, or Matisse Rosary Chapel, the illuminated quarry in Les Baux, and the town where the gypsies celebrate their annual festival.<br><br>When opening this novel and reading the first pages, I immediately realized the importance of the places where the story takes place, literally. <i>La gloire de mon père</i> is the first volume of a tetralogy in which Marcel Pagnol remembers his childhood and youth. Those memories are entrenched in the <b>Aubagne</b> region as much as in his mind and in the pages he has written, and so I proceeded to signal them in My Provence: Cassis, St Loup, La Ciotat, and <b>The Garlaban</b> mountain, which tops this review, and with which Pagnol begins his tale – even though I would not visit them, with the exception of the Sainte-Victoire mountain. In the pages they became as real as the places on which I was walking, so they also belonged to My Provence.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467475002i/19597420._SX540_.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>This was not the first time I read the book. As I had tackled it in my youth, during a summer, since Summers were for reading French. During the recent reading then I began to mix Pagnol’s childhood memories with my own, and realise that various epochs intermingled – Pagnol’s youth happened much before mine, but mine was happening during his adulthood close to the time he wrote the tetralogy.<br><br>I use to think of this series as early samples of what we now call YA literature, and have given them to the girl of a friend of mine not long ago. But in this second reading I no longer conceive of them as particularly fit for youth. No, they are for adults with a nostalgic past.<br><br>For this is a glorious read. The sweetness and the humour are balanced and condensed as if in a flask one could bottle the fragrance of fresh lavender plunged into the brightness of a joyful sky. For the recollection of past memories, and filial love, retains the ingeniousness of childhood with the clarity of a clairvoyant adult.<br><br>My reading continues with the following volumes.<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="1820641288687208874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1686220813" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1686220813" />
    <a title="Steve" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17433080-steve"><img alt="Steve" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420185854p2/17433080.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1686220813?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve" href="/user/show/17433080-steve">Steve</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17433080-steve?shelf=french">french</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1686220813" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10978908060348451657"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474567868i/20617511._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> <i><br/>Marcel Pagnol (1895-1974)<br/> </i><br/> <br/>In 1957 the playwright, cinéaste and film producer Marcel Pagnol published what he called in the <i>Avant-propos</i> his first piece of prose (aside from <i>quelques modestes essais</i>), <i>La gloire de mon père</i> (The Glory of My Father), which opened a tetralogy of memoirs from his childhood and youth - <i>Souvenirs d'enfance</i> - to a well justified popularity. Though Pagnol had been elected to the Académie française in 1946, this charming text is the opposite of the stuffy and studiously</span>
  <span id="freeText10978908060348451657" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474567868i/20617511._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <i><br>Marcel Pagnol (1895-1974)<br> </i><br> <br>In 1957 the playwright, cinéaste and film producer Marcel Pagnol published what he called in the <i>Avant-propos</i> his first piece of prose (aside from <i>quelques modestes essais</i>), <i>La gloire de mon père</i> (The Glory of My Father), which opened a tetralogy of memoirs from his childhood and youth - <i>Souvenirs d'enfance</i> - to a well justified popularity. Though Pagnol had been elected to the Académie française in 1946, this charming text is the opposite of the stuffy and studiously serious memoir one might expect from an Académicien.<br> <br>With loving detail and somewhat exaggerated effect Pagnol recreates life and family in the Provence early in the 20th century - Aubagne, Saint-Loup, Marseille - a life I still saw traces of when I lived in Aix-en-Provence and Marseille in the 80's. I can best give you a sense of this amused, slightly hyperbolic style with a <i>tout petit</i> example in which he describes his little brother, Paul:<br> <i><br>...on le voyait tout à coup s'avancer, titubant, les bras écartés, la figure violette. Il était en train de mourir suffoqué.<br> <br>Ma mère affolée frappait dans son dos, enfonçait un doigt dans sa gorge, ou le secouait en le tenant par les talons, comme fit jadis la mère d'Achille.<br> <br>Alors dans un râle affreux, il expulsait une grosse olive noire, un noyau de pêche, ou une longue lanière de lard.<br> <br>Après quoi, il reprenait ses jeux solitaires, accroupi comme un gros crapaud.</i>(*)<br> <br>A trip to a junk shop becomes an elaborate adventure and generator of reader's chuckles, which effects are soon totally eclipsed by those of a <i>féerique</i> removal to a summer vacation villa in the Provençal countryside full of ancient olive, almond and apricot trees, wild herbs and the buzz of countless cicadas. Indeed, the tone of much of the book is that of an accomplished raconteur entertaining friends gathered around a few bottles of wine with tales of people and places all present know well and love, deliberately told in a manner to widen the eyes of the children at hand. I recommend that you pour a glass and edge into the circle of listeners yourself.<br> <br> <br>(*) ...one saw him suddenly advance, staggering, arms outstretched, face violet. He was in the process of choking to death. My panic-stricken mother pounded on his back, stuck a finger down his throat or shook him upside down by his heels as once did Achilles' mother. Then with a horrible groan he expelled a large black olive, a peach pit or a long lanyard of lard. After which he resumed his solitary games squatting like a great toad.<br> <br> <br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474567868i/20617512._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <i><br>Mont Ventoux</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10978908060348451657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1354589310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1354589310" />
    <a title="Gabrielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6753400-gabrielle"><img alt="Gabrielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598976963p2/6753400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1354589310?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabrielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabrielle" href="/user/show/6753400-gabrielle">Gabrielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=french">french</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=mandatory-reading">mandatory-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=desert-island">desert-island</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=own-a-copy">own-a-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1354589310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7652722994222047847">This series of books are probably my most cherished books. I was a solitary, very bookish child, but the first time I read Marcel Pagnol’s childhood memoirs (I think I was about 6), they cracked my mind open and made me realize that books were so much more than just pretty stories. You can make language do wonderful things, evoke incredible feelings and make your senses travel in very faraway places you would have never imagined. Those books are little treasures in and of themselves, but as they</span>
  <span id="freeText7652722994222047847" style="display:none">This series of books are probably my most cherished books. I was a solitary, very bookish child, but the first time I read Marcel Pagnol’s childhood memoirs (I think I was about 6), they cracked my mind open and made me realize that books were so much more than just pretty stories. You can make language do wonderful things, evoke incredible feelings and make your senses travel in very faraway places you would have never imagined. Those books are little treasures in and of themselves, but as they also opened my mind and turned my love for books into a burning passion, they have earned a spot at the top of my “you absolutely should read this” list.<br /><br />“My father’s glory” and “My mother’s castle” are wonderful at any age. As I re-read them, I find different meanings and different stories to a text I almost know by heart. I used to see stories of playing in the hills, catching cicadas, and going on hunting trips… Now that I am older, I see Marcel’s relationship with his parents and family in a whole new way, and the novels have acquired a new level of beauty and meaning .<br /><br />The synopsis of “a man recalls his younger years and describes growing up and coming of age in turn-of-the-century Provence” doesn’t do this luminous book any justice. These stories will remind you what it was like to see the world through a child’s eyes, that there is so much joy to be found in the simple things and that you should tell the people you care for that you love them every day.<br /><br />I have read those books in French (many time), then in English, to vet the translation (which isn’t bad, but as a friend once said “These books are worth learning to read French for”; chew on that!), as I wanted my non-French-speaking boyfriend to read them and understand what they meant to me. I also dragged him to Marseille, and to the tiny cemetery of La Treille where Pagnol is buried, because I wanted to see with my own eyes the city and landscapes I had been reading about my whole life. That is how much I love these books and how strongly I recommended them to everyone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7652722994222047847" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16554249759968252771" style="display:none">Sometimes you only have to observe a family during one of the many occasions that they're complete and interacting with each other to know what their past was, what they are today and what they will be in the future. <div id="review_249311058" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781589770461" href="/book/show/2148695.La_Gloire_De_Mon_P_re">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5611008-kay?shelf=quirky">quirky</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5611008-kay?shelf=vive-la-france">vive-la-france</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer249311058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1272694428752827369">Read this in French. Pagnol's descriptions of Provence were calming and lovely, and it makes me wish I could just pack up and go on a hunting trip to Provence. Plot-wise, the novel presents an interesting view on growing up and the changing perceptions of parents that results with age. However, I didn't feel very connected with young Marcel, though I could generally relate to his experiences. <br/><br/>I may read it again in English, and perhaps my rating will change. Until then, <b>2.5 stars</b>. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2264309353" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2264309353" />
    <a title="Stephen Durrant" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1457001-stephen-durrant"><img alt="Stephen Durrant" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362701086p2/1457001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2264309353?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen Durrant" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen Durrant" href="/user/show/1457001-stephen-durrant">Stephen Durrant</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2264309353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1051853073921506111">Pagnol’s “La gloire de mon pere” is delicious from beginning to end. It is a story of the loss of innocence, but one with a gentle, human touch that will keep a smile on your face. After discovering his own idealized father’s feet of clay appear, young Marcel, the narrator, loves him all the more (216). And, after finishing the book, there is the fun of the 1990 Yves Robert movie, which is, except for a segment toward the end, a faithful reproduction of the book. Now, a word about the French for</span>
  <span id="freeText1051853073921506111" style="display:none">Pagnol’s “La gloire de mon pere” is delicious from beginning to end. It is a story of the loss of innocence, but one with a gentle, human touch that will keep a smile on your face. After discovering his own idealized father’s feet of clay appear, young Marcel, the narrator, loves him all the more (216). And, after finishing the book, there is the fun of the 1990 Yves Robert movie, which is, except for a segment toward the end, a faithful reproduction of the book. Now, a word about the French for those of you, like me, who still struggle with this language: the major difficulty with reading this in French is the richness of the vocabulary, especially the vocabulary for the material world. Pagnol’s beloved Aubagne is described in rich detail, so that many of the names of plants and animals will send you scurrying to a dictionary . . . necessarily a very large dictionary! In another chapter, Uncle Jules and Marcel’s father Joseph prepare their hunting expedition, so be prepared for a barrage of vocabulary about guns, shells, and various articles of the hunter’s garb and other chapters concern similar activities and technical details. But the story sweeps one along, and a restless foreign language reader like me can just say to himself, I won’t worry too much about what this particular bird or plant or object really is, because often once you know the English equivalent, you still might be as baffled as you were by the French word anyway. At any rate, I see much, much more Pagnol in my readerly future! </span>
  <a data-text-id="1051853073921506111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1244294847" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1244294847" />
    <a title="Frumenty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15745392-frumenty"><img alt="Frumenty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383593740p2/15745392.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1244294847?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Frumenty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Frumenty" href="/user/show/15745392-frumenty">Frumenty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9782877060509" href="/book/show/889842.La_gloire_de_mon_p_re">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15745392-frumenty?shelf=french">french</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1244294847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13868797507598799453">La gloire de mon père / Marcel Pagnol (Souvenirs d'enfance 1)<br/>Le chateau de ma mère / Marcel Pagnol (Souvenirs d'enfance 2)<br/><br/>These two little books are a memoir of the author's childhood, in an age and a society that were perhaps swept away forever by the Great War. Much of what takes place in the books is confined to a period of little more than a year that apparently marked Pagnol's tastes and character for life. There is an idyllic quality about the books, and much that is humorous, to both of w</span>
  <span id="freeText13868797507598799453" style="display:none">La gloire de mon père / Marcel Pagnol (Souvenirs d'enfance 1)<br />Le chateau de ma mère / Marcel Pagnol (Souvenirs d'enfance 2)<br /><br />These two little books are a memoir of the author's childhood, in an age and a society that were perhaps swept away forever by the Great War. Much of what takes place in the books is confined to a period of little more than a year that apparently marked Pagnol's tastes and character for life. There is an idyllic quality about the books, and much that is humorous, to both of which factors I suppose they owe their immense popularity. Pagnol has made it quite explicit that the books were intended for children, but like all the best children's books they can be read with pleasure by adults too.<br /><br />The location is Marseille and its wild mountainous hinterland. The young Marcel's father is both product and representative of French republican schooling, a teacher with a sacred mission to warn French children of the three great enemies of the people: clergy, monarchy and alcohol. The books are peopled with simple folk to whom a humble schoolteacher is a learned man. Pagnol's little family is a microcosm of French society, with his father Joseph advocating for the ideals of the Revolution and his uncle Jules the pious and more worldly Roman Catholic. The wives must be ever vigilant in steering their husbands away from the shoals of ideological conflict. The two men are united in their love of family and of hunting, and the passion for hunting and trapping is the mainspring of the books' interest but also, I think, what dates them; the wholesale slaughter of small animals must make the modern reader wonder, while nobody in the books ever gives the matter a thought.<br /><br />The climactic event of La gloire de mon père is the transformation of Joseph from tyro shooter to legendary hunter who has brought down two rare and highly prized «bartavelles», in two successive shots and on the first day of his first season. Le chateau de ma mère continues the same glorious summer with Marcel's encounter with a new friend, Lili, the son of a carter and a great repository of local knowledge. The boys' days of running wild together in the scrubby hills have the charm of many a children's book of daytime adventure rounded out with evenings of hot meals, maternal love and warm beds. Sadly it must end and the city families must return to Marseille to begin a new school year. The latter half of Le chateau de ma mère is a tale of cramming at school while longing to return to this Eden in the rocky hills, and of a potentially disastrous misadventure on the way back. Two short final chapters wind up the narrative in such a summary fashion that is difficult to imagine how Pagnol managed to add another two volumes of memoirs to the series; and I have decided that the two I have read are quite satisfactory as they are so I will read no more for now. I have other books to read in French.<br /><br />As a memoir of youth these do not compare well with Simone de Beauvoir's Mémoire d'une jeune fille rangée. They lack the gravitas and the spirit of rigorous enquiry of that book. They are written to amuse children, in particular, and they are an affectionate tribute to his parents, but that is all. But as children's books they are very good. Three stars or four? I think four.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13868797507598799453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer698721258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1316682923116287967">This memoir, by the man who created the story "Jean de Florette," tells of his childhood in 1920s Provence. It is vividly written and really brings the time and region to life. Also, parts of it are really funny, as he shows how a young child interprets the world of adults. The one thing I didn't like were some passages where he and his brother amuse themselves in the garden by torturing insects, and where his father goes hunting for a very rare bird. (I'm not against hunting per se, but I am op</span>
  <span id="freeText1316682923116287967" style="display:none">This memoir, by the man who created the story "Jean de Florette," tells of his childhood in 1920s Provence. It is vividly written and really brings the time and region to life. Also, parts of it are really funny, as he shows how a young child interprets the world of adults. The one thing I didn't like were some passages where he and his brother amuse themselves in the garden by torturing insects, and where his father goes hunting for a very rare bird. (I'm not against hunting per se, but I am opposed to killing rare or endangered animals.) Granted, it was a different time and place, but I am a modern reader, and those parts bothered me.</span>

<div id="review_2510736363" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2510736363" />
    <a title="Charlie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22451092-charlie"><img alt="Charlie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595429567p2/22451092.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2510736363?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlie" href="/user/show/22451092-charlie">Charlie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9782266000314" href="/book/show/1484159.La_gloire_de_mon_p_re">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2510736363" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6890567110935187340">My mother absolutely loves Pagnol, she has nearly all of his books and re-reads them often. I was never too excited about the idea of his writing. Perhaps because I am not big on humorous books, or maybe because he talks about a way of life I am already familiar with having grown up in villages/towns from south of France. <br/>Nonetheless, I thought to perfect my french literary culture I finally had to give his books a go. I am unsure that starting with a memoir -of sorts- was in my best interst but</span>
  <span id="freeText6890567110935187340" style="display:none">My mother absolutely loves Pagnol, she has nearly all of his books and re-reads them often. I was never too excited about the idea of his writing. Perhaps because I am not big on humorous books, or maybe because he talks about a way of life I am already familiar with having grown up in villages/towns from south of France. <br />Nonetheless, I thought to perfect my french literary culture I finally had to give his books a go. I am unsure that starting with a memoir -of sorts- was in my best interst but as I predicted, I did not love it.<br />There are some seriously hilarious turn of phrases and he is great at creating atmosphere, but I personally could not care about his early life in Provence,is father's hunting and his curious interest in insects. <br /><br />Well written but just not my cup of tea. I will however try another book of his soon enough. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6890567110935187340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3842413" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3842413" />
    <a title="Cathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/237893-cathryn"><img alt="Cathryn" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3842413?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cathryn" href="/user/show/237893-cathryn">Cathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/237893-cathryn?shelf=goodstuff">goodstuff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3842413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15744328260865025027">This is a great story of and homage to Marcel Pagnol's dad. The prose is both clever and childlike as Pagnol explores his relationship with his father through the eyes of himself as a child. It's also been adapted into a great movie, "My Father's Glory". I'd recommend this book in English and in French.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1190840729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7471302946531058409">Autobiography, Marcel Pagnol's childhood, spent in the South of France. It's a very touching, and often funny, family portrait. The end of the book is mostly about his father, Joseph, a primary school teacher at the beginning of the 20th centuray, and also, a beginner hunter. Recommended for anyone who wants a relatively easy read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UnxyCH944ay8ZGh8Ozco/k1xEto1HueNlV5SKlGDz9zfEQT9jK9qS8RTUVMuO9oVe9duKkz7B4DBzvg8nytE1g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oFGS2jwpKBEdFHMNhmclWa2eNiuAD4Qm77KyhPEQZ2ItPOQvz/6j9mUjSiKTa9eymzhK2/nqZCu7IhiSP7jsaA==')})
  }
//]]>

Nous sommes en 1314 et la prophétie va se réaliser : pendant plus d\'un demi-siècle, les rois se succèdent sur le trône de France, mais n\'y restent jamais bien longtemps. D\'intrigues de palais en morts subites, de révolutions dynastiques en guerres meurtrières, c\'est la valse des rois maudits... L\'avenir de la France se joue pendant ces quelques années noires, période trouble de l\'Histoire. Une époque extraordinaire, jamais ennuyeuse, comme romanesque... L\'auteur l\'a bien compris, lui qui conte les histoires secrètes du royaume et des hommes, de leurs passions comme de leurs faiblesses qui bien souvent bouleversèrent le sort de la France. Académicien, Maurice Druon a rencontré un vif succès avec ces Rois maudits dont l\'adaptation pour le petit écran a marqué des générations de téléspectateurs. --Karla Manuele <\/span>\n  <a
